class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Ethnic_groups"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ethnic groups</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Languages"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Languages</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Tourism"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Tourism</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Financial_services"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Financial services</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Architecture"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Architecture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Literature"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-43"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-45"><a href="#Holidays_and_festivals"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Holidays and festivals</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The first historical evidence of the existence of an island now known as Mauritius is on a map produced by the <a href="/wiki/Italian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian people">Italian</a> cartographer Alberto Cantino in 1502.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> From this, it appears that Mauritius was first named <i>Dina Arobi</i> around 975 by <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arab</a> sailors, the first people to visit the island.\n</p><p>In 1507, Portuguese sailors visited the uninhabited island. The island appears with a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> name <i>Cirne</i> on early Portuguese maps, probably from the name of a ship in the 1507 expedition. Another Portuguese sailor, <a href="/wiki/Dom_(title)" title="Dom (title)">Dom</a> <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mascarenhas" title="Pedro Mascarenhas">Pedro Mascarenhas</a>, gave the name <i><a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarenes</a></i> to the Archipelago.\n</p><p>In 1598, a Dutch squadron under <a href="/wiki/Admiral" title="Admiral">Admiral</a> Wybrand van Warwyck landed at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Port">Grand Port</a> and named the island <i>Mauritius</i>, in honour of <a href="/wiki/Maurice,_Prince_of_Orange" title="Maurice, Prince of Orange">Prince Maurice van Nassau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stadholder" class="mw-redirect" title="Stadholder">stadholder</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>. Later the island became a French colony and was renamed <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a>. On 3 December 1810, the French surrendered the island to Great Britain during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. Under British rule, the island\'s name reverted to <i>Mauritius</i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xca\x83/: &#39;sh&#39; in &#39;shy&#39;">\xca\x83</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Mauritius.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/En-us-Mauritius.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Mauritius.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>. Mauritius is also commonly known as <i>Maurice</i> (<small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[m\xc9\x94\xcb\x88\xca\x81is]</a></span>) and <i>\xc3\x8ele Maurice</i> in French, <i>Moris</i> (pronounced <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole_phonology" title="Mauritian Creole phonology">[mo\xca\x81is]</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Mauritian Creole</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Mauritius" title="History of Mauritius">History of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cantino_planisphere_(1502).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Cantino_planisphere_%281502%29.jpg/450px-Cantino_planisphere_%281502%29.jpg" width="450" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Cantino_planisphere_%281502%29.jpg/675px-Cantino_planisphere_%281502%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Cantino_planisphere_%281502%29.jpg/900px-Cantino_planisphere_%281502%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10643" data-file-height="4998" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cantino_planisphere_(1502).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cantino planisphere (1502), <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Estense" title="Biblioteca Estense">Biblioteca Estense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modena" title="Modena">Modena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The island of Mauritius was uninhabited before its first recorded visit during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> by <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arab</a> sailors, who named it Dina Arobi. However, the island might have been visited well before by sailors of ancient times; wax tablets were found on the shores of Mauritius by the Dutch, but since the tablets were not preserved, it cannot be said whether they were of <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> or Arab origin.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1507, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> sailors came to the uninhabited island and established a visiting base. <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Fernandes_Pereira" title="Diogo Fernandes Pereira">Diogo Fernandes Pereira</a>, a Portuguese navigator, was the first European known to land in Mauritius. He named the island "Ilha do Cirne". The Portuguese did not stay long as they were not interested in these islands.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Dutch_Mauritius_.281638.E2.80.931710.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_Mauritius_(1638\xe2\x80\x931710)">Dutch Mauritius (1638\xe2\x80\x931710)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Dutch Mauritius (1638\xe2\x80\x931710)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mauritius" title="Dutch Mauritius">Dutch Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg/220px-Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg/330px-Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg/440px-Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1716" data-file-height="1506" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Van_Keulen_-_De_Z._O._Haven_van_%27t_Eyland_Mauritius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch map of a coast of Mauritius. The Dutch were the first to establish a <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mauritius" title="Dutch Mauritius">permanent human settlement in Mauritius</a>. Dutch colonists named it after <a href="/wiki/Maurice_of_Nassau" class="mw-redirect" title="Maurice of Nassau">Maurice of Nassau</a>, Prince of Orange and the <a href="/wiki/Stadtholder" title="Stadtholder">Stadtholder</a> of the Dutch Republic.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg/220px-School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg" width="220" height="297" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg/330px-School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg/440px-School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1100" data-file-height="1483" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:School_of_Michiel_Jansz._van_Mierevelt_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maurice,_Prince_of_Orange" title="Maurice, Prince of Orange">Maurice, Prince of Orange</a>, after whom the Island was named.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1598 a Dutch squadron under Admiral Wybrand Van Warwyck landed at <a href="/wiki/Grand_Port" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Port">Grand Port</a> and named the island "Mauritius" after <a href="/wiki/Maurice,_Prince_of_Orange" title="Maurice, Prince of Orange">Prince Maurice van Nassau</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch Republic</a>, the ruler of his country. The Dutch established a small colony on the island in 1638, from which they exploited <a href="/wiki/Ebony" title="Ebony">ebony</a> trees and introduced <a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">sugar cane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_animals" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic animals">domestic animals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>. It was from here that Dutch navigator <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> set out to discover the western part of Australia. The first Dutch settlement lasted twenty years. Several attempts were subsequently made, but the settlements never developed enough to produce dividends, causing the Dutch to abandon Mauritius in 1710.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="French_Mauritius_.281715.E2.80.931810.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Mauritius_(1715\xe2\x80\x931810)">French Mauritius (1715\xe2\x80\x931810)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: French Mauritius (1715\xe2\x80\x931810)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France (Mauritius)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg/220px-Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg/330px-Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg/440px-Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1256" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais_Statue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A statute of <a href="/wiki/Bertrand-Fran%C3%A7ois_Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais" title="Bertrand-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mah\xc3\xa9 de La Bourdonnais">Bertrand-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mah\xc3\xa9 de La Bourdonnais</a></div></div></div>\n<p>France, which already controlled neighbouring \xc3\x8ele Bourbon (now <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R\xc3\xa9union">R\xc3\xa9union</a>), took control of Mauritius in 1715 and renamed it <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a>. In 1723, the <a href="/wiki/Code_Noir" title="Code Noir">Code Noir</a> was established to categorise one group of human beings as "goods", in order for the owner of these goods to be able to obtain insurance money and compensation in case of loss of his "goods".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The 1735 arrival of French governor <a href="/wiki/Bertrand-Fran%C3%A7ois_Mah%C3%A9_de_La_Bourdonnais" title="Bertrand-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mah\xc3\xa9 de La Bourdonnais">Bertrand-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mah\xc3\xa9 de La Bourdonnais</a> coincided with development of a prosperous economy based on sugar production. Mah\xc3\xa9 de La Bourdonnais established <a href="/wiki/Port_Louis" title="Port Louis">Port Louis</a> as a naval base and a shipbuilding centre.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Under his governorship, numerous buildings were erected, a number of which are still standing. These include part of Government House, the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Mon_Plaisir" class="mw-redirect" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teau de Mon Plaisir">Ch\xc3\xa2teau de Mon Plaisir</a>, and the Line Barracks, the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Police_Force" title="Mauritius Police Force">police force</a>. The island was under the administration of the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a> which maintained its presence until 1767.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 1767 to 1810, except for a brief period during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> when the inhabitants set up a government virtually independent of France, the island was controlled by officials appointed by the <a href="/wiki/French_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="French Government">French Government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Henri_Bernardin_de_Saint-Pierre" title="Jacques-Henri Bernardin de Saint-Pierre">Jacques-Henri Bernardin de Saint-Pierre</a> lived on the island from 1768 to 1771, then went back to France, where he wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_et_Virginie" title="Paul et Virginie">Paul et Virginie</a></i>, a love story, which made the Isle de France famous wherever the French language was spoken. Two famous French governors were the Vicomte de Souillac (who constructed the Chauss\xc3\xa9e in Port Louis<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint2_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint2-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and encouraged farmers to settle in the district of Savanne), and <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Bruni_d%27Entrecasteaux" title="Antoine Bruni d&#39;Entrecasteaux">Antoine Bruni d\'Entrecasteaux</a> (who saw to it that the French in the Indian Ocean should have their headquarters in Mauritius instead of <a href="/wiki/Pondicherry" title="Pondicherry">Pondicherry</a> in India).<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Charles_Mathieu_Isidore_Decaen" title="Charles Mathieu Isidore Decaen">Charles Mathieu Isidore Decaen</a> was a successful general in the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> and, in some ways, a rival of <a href="/wiki/Napol%C3%A9on_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napol\xc3\xa9on I">Napol\xc3\xa9on I</a>. He ruled as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Governor of Isle de France (Mauritius)">Governor of Isle de France</a> and R\xc3\xa9union from 1803 to 1810. British naval <a href="/wiki/Cartographer" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartographer">cartographer</a> and explorer <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Flinders" title="Matthew Flinders">Matthew Flinders</a> was arrested and detained by General Decaen on the island, in contravention of an order from Napol\xc3\xa9on. During the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, Mauritius became a base from which <a href="/wiki/French_corsairs" title="French corsairs">French corsairs</a> organised successful raids on British commercial ships. The raids continued until 1810, when a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> expedition led by <a href="/wiki/Commodore_(Royal_Navy)" title="Commodore (Royal Navy)">Commodore</a> <a href="/wiki/Josias_Rowley" title="Josias Rowley">Josias Rowley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">R.N.</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Irish">Anglo-Irish</a> <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy_(class)" title="Aristocracy (class)">aristocrat</a>, was sent to capture the island. Despite winning the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grand_Port" title="Battle of Grand Port">Battle of Grand Port</a>, the only French naval victory over the British during these wars, the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_%C3%8Ele_de_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of \xc3\x8ele de France">French could not prevent the British from landing</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cap_Malheureux" title="Cap Malheureux">Cap Malheureux</a> three months later. They formally surrendered the island on the fifth day of the invasion, 3 December 1810,<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> on terms allowing settlers to keep their land and property and to use the French language and law of France in criminal and civil matters. Under British rule, the island\'s name reverted to Mauritius.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="British_Mauritius_.281810.E2.80.931968.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Mauritius_(1810\xe2\x80\x931968)">British Mauritius (1810\xe2\x80\x931968)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: British Mauritius (1810\xe2\x80\x931968)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Mauritius" title="British Mauritius">British Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg/300px-Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg" width="300" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg/450px-Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg/600px-Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3465" data-file-height="2192" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Combat_de_Grand_Port_mg_9425.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grand_Port" title="Battle of Grand Port">Battle of Grand Port</a> between French and British naval forces, 1810</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg/300px-Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg" width="300" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg/450px-Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg/600px-Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="708" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Numa_Desjardins_Champ_de_Mars_Port_Louis_1880.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse" title="Champ de Mars Racecourse">Champ de Mars Racecourse</a>, Port Louis, 1880</div></div></div>\n<p>The British administration, which began with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Townsend_Farquhar" title="Robert Townsend Farquhar">Sir Robert Farquhar</a> as <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_British_Mauritius" title="Governor of British Mauritius">Governor</a>, led to rapid social and economic changes. However, it was tainted by the Ratsitatane episode. Ratsitatane, nephew of King Radama of Madagascar, was brought to Mauritius as a political prisoner. He managed to escape from prison and plotted a rebellion that would free the island\'s slaves. He was betrayed by an associate and was caught by the British forces, summarily judged, and condemned to death. He was beheaded at Plaine Verte on 15 April 1822, and his head was displayed as a deterrent against future uprisings among the slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-Selvon_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selvon-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1832, Adrien d\'\xc3\x89pinay launched the first Mauritian newspaper (<i>Le Cern\xc3\xa9en</i>) which was not controlled by the government. In the same year, there was a move by the procureur-general to abolish slavery without compensation to the slave owners. This gave rise to discontent, and, to check an eventual rebellion, the government ordered all the inhabitants to surrender their arms. Furthermore, a stone fortress, Fort Adelaide, was built on a hill (now known as the Citadel hill) in the centre of Port Louis to quell any uprising.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint2_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint2-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slave_population_graph.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Slave_population_graph.png/220px-Slave_population_graph.png" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Slave_population_graph.png/330px-Slave_population_graph.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Slave_population_graph.png/440px-Slave_population_graph.png 2x" data-file-width="668" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Slave_population_graph.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Demographics of slaves in Mauritius (top line represents death rate)</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> was abolished in 1835, and the planters ultimately received two million pounds sterling in compensation for the loss of their slaves who had been imported from Africa and Madagascar during the French occupation. The <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">abolition of slavery</a> had important impacts on Mauritius\'s society, economy and population. The planters brought a large number of <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured servant">indentured labourers</a> from India to work in the sugar cane fields. Between 1834 and 1921, around half a million indentured labourers were present on the island. They worked on sugar estates, factories, in transport and on construction sites. Additionally, the British brought 8,740 <a href="/wiki/Indian_people" title="Indian people">Indian</a> soldiers to the island.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_19-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Aapravasi_Ghat" title="Aapravasi Ghat">Aapravasi Ghat</a>, in the bay at <a href="/wiki/Port_Louis" title="Port Louis">Port Louis</a> and now a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> site, was the first British <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> to serve as a major reception centre for <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servants" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured servants">indentured servants</a>.\n</p><p>An important figure of the 19th century was <a href="/w/index.php?title=R%C3%A9my_Ollier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="R\xc3\xa9my Ollier (page does not exist)">R\xc3\xa9my Ollier</a>, a journalist of mixed origin. In 1828, the colour bar was officially abolished in Mauritius, but British governors gave little power to coloured persons, and appointed only whites as leading officials. R\xc3\xa9my Ollier petitioned to <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> to allow coloureds in the council of government, and this became possible a few years later. He also made Port Louis become a municipality so that the citizens could administer the town through their own elected representatives. A street has been named after him in Port Louis, and his bust was erected in the Jardin de la Compagnie in 1906.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1885 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius_(1885)" title="Constitution of Mauritius (1885)">a new constitution</a> was introduced to Mauritius. It created elected positions on the governing council, but the franchise was restricted mainly to the French and Creole classes.\n</p><p>The labourers brought from India were not always fairly treated, and a German, Adolph von Plevitz, made himself the unofficial protector of these immigrants. He mixed with many of the labourers, and in 1871 helped them to write a petition which was sent to <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Hamilton-Gordon,_1st_Baron_Stanmore" title="Arthur Hamilton-Gordon, 1st Baron Stanmore">Governor Gordon</a>. A commission was appointed to look into the complaints made by the Indian immigrants, and in 1872 two lawyers, appointed by the British Crown, were sent from England to make an inquiry. This Royal Commission recommended several measures that would affect the lives of Indian labourers during the next fifty years.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sugar_Estate_Tractor_1901.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sugar_Estate_Tractor_1901.jpg/220px-Sugar_Estate_Tractor_1901.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Sugar_Estate_Tractor_1901.jpg/330px-Sugar_Estate_Tractor_1901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a2/Sugar_Estate_Tractor_1901.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="319" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sugar_Estate_Tractor_1901.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A sugar tractor in 1901 belonging to A G Hossen and Company, an Indo-Mauritian firm in the colonial period</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg/220px-Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg/330px-Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg/440px-Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Mauritius_1923.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British colonial flag, 1923</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg/220px-Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg/330px-Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg/440px-Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamp_Mauritius_1954_5c.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Postage stamp with portrait of Queen Elizabeth II, 1954</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guy_Forget.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Guy_Forget.jpg/220px-Guy_Forget.jpg" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Guy_Forget.jpg/330px-Guy_Forget.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Guy_Forget.jpg/440px-Guy_Forget.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guy_Forget.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A public rally in 1965</div></div></div>\n<p>In November 1901, <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a> visited Mauritius, on his way from South Africa to India. He stayed on the island for two weeks, and urged the Indo-Mauritian community to take an interest in education and to play a more active role in politics. Back in India, he sent over a young lawyer, <a href="/wiki/Manilal_Doctor" title="Manilal Doctor">Manilal Doctor</a>, to improve the plight of the Indo-Mauritians. During the same year, faster links were established with the island of Rodrigues thanks to the wireless.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1903, motorcars were introduced in Mauritius, and in 1910 the first taxis, operated by Joseph Merven, came into service. The electrification of Port Louis took place in 1909, and in the same decade the Mauritius Hydro Electric Company (managed by the Atchia Brothers) was authorised to provide power to the towns of upper Plaines Wilhems.\n</p><p>The 1910s were a period of political agitation. The rising middle class (made up of doctors, lawyers, and teachers) began to challenge the political power of the sugar cane landowners. Dr. Eug\xc3\xa8ne Laurent, mayor of Port Louis, was the leader of this new group; his party, Action Lib\xc3\xa9rale, demanded that more people should be allowed to vote in the elections. Action Lib\xc3\xa9rale was opposed by the Parti de l\'Ordre, led by Henri Lecl\xc3\xa9zio, the most influential of the sugar magnates.<sup id="cite_ref-Toussaint_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toussaint-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1911 there were riots in Port Louis due to a false rumour that Dr. Eug\xc3\xa8ne Laurent had been murdered by the oligarchs in Curepipe. Shops and offices were damaged in the capital, and one person was killed. In the same year, 1911, the first public cinema shows took place in Curepipe, and, in the same town, a stone building was erected to house the Royal College.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1912, a wider telephone network came into service, and it was used by the government, business firms, and a few private households.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> broke out in August 1914. Many Mauritians volunteered to fight in Europe against the Germans and in <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> against the Turks. But the war affected Mauritius much less than the wars of the eighteenth century. On the contrary, the 1914\xe2\x80\x9318 war was a period of great prosperity because of a boom in sugar prices. In 1919 the Mauritius Sugar Syndicate came into being, and it included 70% of all sugar producers.\n</p><p>The 1920s saw the rise of a "retrocessionism" movement which favoured the retrocession of Mauritius to France. The movement rapidly collapsed because none of the candidates who wanted Mauritius to be given back to France was elected in the 1921 elections. Due to the post-war recession, there was a sharp drop in sugar prices. Many sugar estates closed down, and it marked the end of an era for the sugar magnates who had not only controlled the economy, but also the political life of the country. Raoul Rivet, the editor of <i>Le Mauricien</i> newspaper, campaigned for a revision of the constitution that would give the emerging middle class a greater role in the running of the country. The principles of <a href="/wiki/Arya_Samaj" title="Arya Samaj">Arya Samaj</a> began to infiltrate the Hindu community, who clamoured for more social justice.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 1930s saw the birth of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Mauritius)" title="Labour Party (Mauritius)">Labour Party</a>, launched by Dr. Maurice Cur\xc3\xa9. <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Anquetil" title="Emmanuel Anquetil">Emmanuel Anquetil</a> rallied the urban workers while Pandit Sahadeo concentrated on the rural working class. The <a href="/wiki/Uba_riots_of_1937" title="Uba riots of 1937">Uba riots of 1937</a> resulted in reforms by the local British government that improved labour conditions and led to the un-banning of labour unions.<sup id="cite_ref-js_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-js-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rg_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  Labour Day was celebrated for the first time in 1938. More than 30,000 workers sacrificed a day\'s wage and came from all over the island to attend a giant meeting at the Champ de Mars.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in 1939, many Mauritians volunteered to serve under the British flag in Africa and the Near East, fighting against the German and Italian armies. Some went to England to become pilots and ground staff in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. Mauritius was never really threatened, but several British ships were sunk outside Port Louis by German submarines in 1943.\n</p><p>During World War II, conditions were hard in the country; the prices of commodities doubled, but the salaries of workers increased only by 10 to 20 percent. There was civil unrest, and the colonial government crushed all trade union activities. However, the labourers of Belle Vue Harel Sugar Estate went on strike on 27 September 1943. Police officers eventually fired on the crowd, and killed three labourers including a boy of ten and a pregnant woman, Anjaly Coopen.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first general elections were held on 9 August 1948 and were won by the Labour Party. This party, led by Guy Rozemont, bettered its position in 1953, and, on the strength of the election results, demanded <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a>. Constitutional conferences were held in London in 1955 and 1957, and the ministerial system was introduced. Voting took place for the first time on the basis of universal adult suffrage on 9 March 1959. The general election was again won by the Labour Party, led this time by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam">Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ram_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ram-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A Constitutional Review Conference was held in London in 1961, and a programme of further constitutional advance was established. The 1963 election was won by the Labour Party and its allies. The <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Office" title="Colonial Office">Colonial Office</a> noted that politics of a communal nature was gaining ground in Mauritius and that the choice of candidates (by parties) and the voting behaviour (of electors) were governed by ethnic and caste considerations.<sup id="cite_ref-ram_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ram-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Around that time, two eminent British academics, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Titmuss" title="Richard Titmuss">Richard Titmuss</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Meade" title="James Meade">James Meade</a>, published a report of the island\'s social problems caused by overpopulation and the monoculture of sugar cane. This led to an intense campaign to halt the population explosion, and the decade registered a sharp decline in population growth.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Independence_.28since_1968.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(since_1968)">Independence (since 1968)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence (since 1968)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_(1968%E2%80%931992)" title="Mauritius (1968\xe2\x80\x931992)">Mauritius (1968\xe2\x80\x931992)</a></div>\n<p>At the Lancaster Conference of 1965, it became clear that Britain wanted to relieve itself of the colony of Mauritius. In 1959, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Macmillan" title="Harold Macmillan">Harold Macmillan</a> had made his famous <i><a href="/wiki/Wind_of_Change_(speech)" title="Wind of Change (speech)">Winds of Change Speech</a></i> where he acknowledged that the best option for Britain was to give complete independence to its colonies. Thus, since the late Fifties, the way was paved for independence.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_(29).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_%2829%29.jpg/220px-Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_%2829%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_%2829%29.jpg/330px-Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_%2829%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_%2829%29.jpg/440px-Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_%2829%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_(29).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A statue in Port Louis of Sir <a href="/wiki/Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam" title="Seewoosagur Ramgoolam">Seewoosagur Ramgoolam</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius" title="Prime Minister of Mauritius">Prime Minister of Mauritius</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:200_rupi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/200_rupi.jpg/220px-200_rupi.jpg" width="220" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/200_rupi.jpg/330px-200_rupi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/200_rupi.jpg/440px-200_rupi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1179" data-file-height="538" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:200_rupi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 200 <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_rupee" title="Mauritian rupee">Mauritian rupee</a> banknote showing the image of Sir <a href="/wiki/Abdool_Razack_Mohamed" title="Abdool Razack Mohamed">Abdool Razack Mohamed</a>, an early leader of independent Mauritius</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG/220px-Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG/330px-Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG/440px-Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius-25rupees-banknote-2003.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Mauritian rupee banknote including a picture of <a href="/wiki/Moilin_Jean_Ah-Chuen" title="Moilin Jean Ah-Chuen">Moilin Jean Ah-Chuen</a>, the country\'s first Sino-Mauritian cabinet minister</div></div></div>\n<p>Later in 1965, after the Lancaster Conference, the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a> was excised from the territory of Mauritius to form the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> (BIOT). A general election took place on 7 August 1967, and the Labour Party and its two allies obtained the majority of seats. In January 1968, six weeks before the declaration of independence the <a href="/wiki/1968_Mauritian_riots" title="1968 Mauritian riots">1968 Mauritian riots</a> occurred in Port Louis leading to the deaths of 25 people.<sup id="cite_ref-mg_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mg-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eisa_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eisa-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mauritius adopted a new constitution and independence was proclaimed on 12 March 1968. Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam became the first prime minister of an independent Mauritius with Queen Elizabeth II remaining head of state as Queen of Mauritius. In 1969, the opposition party <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Militant_Movement" title="Mauritian Militant Movement">Mauritian Militant Movement</a> (MMM) led by <a href="/wiki/Paul_B%C3%A9renger" title="Paul B\xc3\xa9renger">Paul B\xc3\xa9renger</a> was founded. Later in 1971, the MMM, backed by unions, called a series of strikes in the port which caused a state of emergency in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The coalition government of the Labour Party and the PMSD (Parti Mauricien Social D\xc3\xa9mocrate) reacted by curtailing civil liberties and curbing freedom of the press.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Two unsuccessful assassination attempts were made against Paul B\xc3\xa9renger. The second one led to the death of Azor Ad\xc3\xa9la\xc3\xafde, a dock worker and activist, on 25 November 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> General elections were postponed and public meetings were prohibited. Members of the MMM including Paul B\xc3\xa9renger were imprisoned on 23 December 1971. The MMM leader was released a year later.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 1975, a student revolt that started at the University of Mauritius swept across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The students were unsatisfied with an education system that did not meet their aspirations and gave limited prospects for future employment. On 20 May, thousands of students tried to enter Port-Louis over the Grand River North West bridge and clashed with police. An act of Parliament was passed on 16 December 1975 to extend the right to vote to 18-year-olds. This was seen as an attempt to appease the frustration of the younger generation.<sup id="cite_ref-Selvon_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selvon-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The next general election took place on 20 December 1976. The Labour Party won 28 seats out of 62<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> but Prime Minister Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam managed to remain in office, with a two-seat majority, after striking an alliance with the PMSD of Gaetan Duval.\n</p><p>In 1982 an MMM government led by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Anerood_Jugnauth" title="Anerood Jugnauth">Anerood Jugnauth</a> and Paul B\xc3\xa9renger as Minister of Finance was elected. However, ideological and personality differences emerged within the MMM leadership. The power struggle between B\xc3\xa9renger and Jugnauth peaked in March 1983. Jugnauth travelled to New Delhi to attend a <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> summit; on his return, B\xc3\xa9renger proposed constitutional changes that would strip power from the Prime Minister. At Jugnauth\'s request, PM <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a> of India planned an armed intervention involving the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Indian Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Army" title="Indian Army">Indian Army</a> to prevent a <a href="/wiki/Coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Coup">coup</a> under the code name <a href="/wiki/Operation_Lal_Dora" title="Operation Lal Dora">Operation Lal Dora</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The MMM government split up nine months after the June 1982 election. According to an Information Ministry official the nine months was a "socialist experiment".<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The new <a href="/wiki/Mouvement_Socialiste_Militant" class="mw-redirect" title="Mouvement Socialiste Militant">MSM</a> party, led by Anerood Jugnauth, was elected in 1983. Ga\xc3\xabtan Duval became the vice-prime minister. Throughout the decade, Anerood Jugnauth ruled the country with the help of the PMSD and the Labour Party.\n</p><p>That period saw a growth in the EPZ (Export Processing Zone) sector. Industrialisation began to spread to villages as well, and attracted young workers from all ethnic communities. As a result, the sugar industry began to lose its hold on the economy. Large retail chains began opening stores opened in 1985 and offered credit facilities to low income earners, thus allowing them to afford basic household appliances. There was also a boom in the tourism industry, and new hotels sprang up throughout the island. In 1989 the stock exchange opened its doors and in 1992 the freeport began operation.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1990, the Prime Minister lost the vote on changing the Constitution to make the country a republic with B\xc3\xa9renger as President.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Republic_.28since_1992.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_(since_1992)">Republic (since 1992)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Republic (since 1992)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 12 March 1992, twenty-four years after independence, Mauritius was proclaimed a republic within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_19-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The last Governor General, <a href="/wiki/Veerasamy_Ringadoo" title="Veerasamy Ringadoo">Sir Veerasamy Ringadoo</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mauritius" title="President of Mauritius">President</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> This was under a transitional arrangement, in which he was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Cassam_Uteem" title="Cassam Uteem">Cassam Uteem</a> later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Political power remained with the Prime Minister.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anerood_jugnauth_n_bush.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Anerood_jugnauth_n_bush.jpg/220px-Anerood_jugnauth_n_bush.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Anerood_jugnauth_n_bush.jpg/330px-Anerood_jugnauth_n_bush.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2a/Anerood_jugnauth_n_bush.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="267" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anerood_jugnauth_n_bush.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mauritian Prime Minister Sir <a href="/wiki/Anerood_Jugnauth" title="Anerood Jugnauth">Anerood Jugnauth</a> meeting U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> at the White House in 2003</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Raymond_Berenger_exchanging_the_documents_after_the_signing_of_agreements_between_two_countries,_in_Port_Louis,_Mauritius_in_Port_Louis,_Mauritius_on_March_31_2005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Paul_Raymond_Berenger_exchanging_the_documents_after_the_signing_of_agreements_between_two_countries%2C_in_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_in_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_on_March_31_2005.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Paul_Raymond_Berenger_exchanging_the_documents_after_the_signing_of_agreements_between_two_countries%2C_in_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_in_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_on_March_31_2005.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Paul_Raymond_Berenger_exchanging_the_documents_after_the_signing_of_agreements_between_two_countries%2C_in_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_in_Port_Louis%2C_Mauritius_on_March_31_2005.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Raymond_Berenger_exchanging_the_documents_after_the_signing_of_agreements_between_two_countries,_in_Port_Louis,_Mauritius_in_Port_Louis,_Mauritius_on_March_31_2005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mauritian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Paul_Berenger" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Berenger">Paul Berenger</a> and Indian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a> exchange agreements in Port  Louis in 2005</div></div></div>\n<p>Despite an improvement in the economy, which coincided with a fall in the price of petrol and a favourable dollar exchange rate, the government did not enjoy full popularity. As early as 1984, there was discontent. Through the Newspapers and Periodicals Amendment Act, the government tried to make every newspaper provide a bank guarantee of half a million rupees. Forty-three journalists protested by participating in a public demonstration in Port Louis, in front of Parliament. They were arrested and freed on bail. This caused a public outcry and the government had to review its policy.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was also dissatisfaction in the education sector. There were not enough high-quality secondary colleges to answer the growing demand of primary school leavers who had got through their CPE (Certificate of Primary Education). In 1991, a master plan for education failed to get national support and contributed to the government\'s downfall.<sup id="cite_ref-Dinan_24-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dinan-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Navin_Ramgoolam" title="Navin Ramgoolam">Navin Ramgoolam</a> was elected as Prime Minister in 1995. In February 1999, the country experienced a <a href="/wiki/1999_Mauritian_riots" title="1999 Mauritian riots">brief period of civil unrest</a>. Riots flared after the popular singer <a href="/wiki/Kaya_(Mauritian_musician)" title="Kaya (Mauritian musician)">Kaya</a>, arrested for smoking marijuana at a public concert, was found dead in his prison cell. President <a href="/wiki/Cassam_Uteem" title="Cassam Uteem">Cassam Uteem</a> and Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Jean_Marg%C3%A9ot" title="Jean Marg\xc3\xa9ot">Jean Marg\xc3\xa9ot</a> toured the country and, after four days of turmoil, calm was restored.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> A commission of enquiry was set up to investigate the root causes of the social disturbance. The resulting report delved into the cause of poverty and qualified many tenacious beliefs as perceptions.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Anerood Jugnauth of the MSM returned to power in 2000 after making an alliance with the MMM. In 2002, the island of <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a> became an autonomous entity within the republic and was thus able to elect its own representatives to administer the island. In 2003, the prime ministership was transferred to Paul B\xc3\xa9renger of the MMM, and Anerood Jugnauth went to Le R\xc3\xa9duit to serve as president. Berenger was the first Franco-Mauritian premier in the country\'s history. In 2005, Navin Ramgoolam and the Labour Party returned to power. Ramgoolam lost power in 2014. He was succeeded by Anerood Jugnauth. \n</p><p>On 21 January 2017, Anerood Jugnauth announced that in two days time he would resign in favour of his son, Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Pravind_Jugnauth" title="Pravind Jugnauth">Pravind Jugnauth</a>, who would assume the office of prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The transition took place as planned on 23 January.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>In 2018, Mauritian president <a href="/wiki/Ameenah_Gurib-Fakim" class="mw-redirect" title="Ameenah Gurib-Fakim">Ameenah Gurib-Fakim</a> (the only erstwhile female head of state in the African Union) resigned over a financial scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Gurib-Fakim faced pressure to resign from Prime Minister Jugnauth and his father.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Truth_and_Justice_Commission">Truth and Justice Commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Truth and Justice Commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Operating from 2009 to 2011 the <a href="/wiki/Truth_and_Justice_Commission" title="Truth and Justice Commission">Truth and Justice Commission</a> was established to explore the impact of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured servant">indentured servitude</a> in Mauritius. The Commission was tasked to investigate the dispossession of land and "determine appropriate measures to be extended to descendants of slaves and indentured laborers."<sup id="cite_ref-:1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> It was "unique in that it [dealt] with socio-economic class abuses" and explored the possibility of reparations.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The Commission attempted to cover more than 370 years, the longest period of time that a truth commission has ever covered.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Published on 25 November 2011, the report outlined over 300 recommendations detailing ways to bring those affected by slavery and indentured labour out of poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (July 2017)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Mauritius" title="Geography of Mauritius">Geography of Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outer_islands_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="Outer islands of Mauritius">Outer islands of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LocationMauritius.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/LocationMauritius.png/220px-LocationMauritius.png" width="220" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/LocationMauritius.png 1.5x" data-file-width="248" data-file-height="117" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LocationMauritius.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Areas under Mauritian sovereignty</div></div></div>\n<p>The total land area of the country is 2,040&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (790&#160;sq&#160;mi) (about 80% the size of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>). It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_total_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by total area">170th largest nation</a> in the world by size. The Republic of Mauritius is constituted of <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Island" title="Mauritius Island">the main island of Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outer_Islands_of_Mauritius" title="Outer Islands of Mauritius">several outlying islands</a>. The second-largest island is <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a> with an area of 108&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (42&#160;sq&#160;mi) and situated 560&#160;km (350&#160;mi) to the east of Mauritius; the twin islands of <a href="/wiki/Agalega" class="mw-redirect" title="Agalega">Agalega</a> with a total land area of 2,600 hectares (26&#160;km<sup>2</sup>; 10&#160;sq&#160;mi) are situated some 1,000&#160;km (620&#160;mi) north of Mauritius. <a href="/wiki/Cargados_Carajos" class="mw-redirect" title="Cargados Carajos">Saint Brandon</a> is an archipelago comprising a number of sand-banks, shoals and islets. It is situated some 430&#160;km (270&#160;mi) northeast of Mauritius and is mostly used as a fishing base by the Raphael Fishing Company Limited.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-territory_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-territory-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The nation\'s <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a> (EEZ) covers about 2.3&#160;million square kilometres (890,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) of the Indian Ocean, including approximately 400,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (150,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) jointly managed with the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mauritius_Island">Mauritius Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mauritius Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Island" title="Mauritius Island">Mauritius Island</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Mauritius.png/600px-Mauritius.png" width="600" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Mauritius.png/900px-Mauritius.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Mauritius.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="435" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A panoramic view of a part of Mauritius Island</div></div></div>\n<p>Mauritius is 2,000&#160;km (1,200&#160;mi) off the southeast coast of Africa, between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_south" title="19th parallel south">19\xc2\xb058.8\'</a> and <a href="/wiki/20th_parallel_south" title="20th parallel south">20\xc2\xb031.7\'</a> south and longitudes <a href="/wiki/57th_meridian_east" title="57th meridian east">57\xc2\xb018.0\'</a> and <a href="/wiki/57th_meridian_east" title="57th meridian east">57\xc2\xb046.5\'</a> east. It is 65&#160;km (40&#160;mi) long and 45&#160;km (30&#160;mi) wide. Its land area is 1,864.8&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (720.0&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The island is surrounded by more than 150&#160;km (100&#160;mi) of white sandy beaches, and the lagoons are protected from the open sea by the world\'s third-largest coral reef, which surrounds the island.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>  Just off the Mauritian coast lie some 49 uninhabited islands and <a href="/wiki/Islets_of_Mauritius" title="Islets of Mauritius">islets</a>, several used as natural reserves for endangered species.\n</p><p>The island of Mauritius is relatively young geologically, having been created by volcanic activity some 8 million years ago. Together with Saint Brandon, R\xc3\xa9union, and Rodrigues, the island is part of the <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Islands" title="Mascarene Islands">Mascarene Islands</a>. These islands have emerged as a result of gigantic underwater volcanic eruptions that happened thousands of kilometres to the east of the continental block made up of Africa and Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-territory_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-territory-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> They are no longer volcanically active and the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union_hotspot" title="R\xc3\xa9union hotspot">hotspot</a> now rests under R\xc3\xa9union Island. Mauritius is encircled by a broken ring of mountain ranges, varying in height from 300\xe2\x80\x93800&#160;m (1,000\xe2\x80\x932,600&#160;ft) above sea level. The land rises from coastal plains to a central plateau where it reaches a height of 670&#160;m (2,200&#160;ft); the highest peak is in the southwest, <a href="/wiki/Piton_de_la_Petite_Rivi%C3%A8re_Noire" title="Piton de la Petite Rivi\xc3\xa8re Noire">Piton de la Petite Rivi\xc3\xa8re Noire</a> at 828 metres (2,717&#160;ft). Streams and rivers speckle the island, many formed in the cracks created by lava flows.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption">Landscapes of Mauritius Island</li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px"><div style="width: 162px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/View_from_Curepipe_-_panoramio.jpg/240px-View_from_Curepipe_-_panoramio.jpg" width="160" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Tamarin.jpg/360px-Tamarin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Tamarin.jpg/480px-Tamarin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tamarin,_Mauritius" title="Tamarin, Mauritius">Tamarin</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 183.33333333333px"><div style="width: 183.33333333333px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width:
