title="Chamarel">Chamarel</a>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts_of_Mauritius_Island">Districts of Mauritius Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Districts of Mauritius Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Mauritius" title="Districts of Mauritius">Districts of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DSCN6349_stitch_(6393865603).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/DSCN6349_stitch_%286393865603%29.jpg/220px-DSCN6349_stitch_%286393865603%29.jpg" width="220" height="361" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/DSCN6349_stitch_%286393865603%29.jpg/330px-DSCN6349_stitch_%286393865603%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/DSCN6349_stitch_%286393865603%29.jpg/440px-DSCN6349_stitch_%286393865603%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3824" data-file-height="6277" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DSCN6349_stitch_(6393865603).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alexandra Waterfall</div></div></div>\n<p>Mauritius is subdivided into nine Districts, they consist of different <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities,_towns_and_villages_in_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities, towns and villages in Mauritius">cities, towns and villages</a>.\n</p>\n<div role="img" class="noresize" style="width: 450px; float: none; clear: none; line-height: 1; text-align: center; background-color: #ffffff; position: relative; max-width: 100%; overflow-x: auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_districts_blank.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Mauritius_districts_blank.svg/450px-Mauritius_districts_blank.svg.png" width="450" height="518" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Mauritius_districts_blank.svg/675px-Mauritius_districts_blank.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Mauritius_districts_blank.svg/900px-Mauritius_districts_blank.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="567" data-file-height="653" /></a> \n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:154px; top:452px"><b><a href="/wiki/Savanne_District" title="Savanne District">Savanne</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:344px; top:232px"><b><a href="/wiki/Flacq_District" title="Flacq District">Flacq</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:82px; top:292px"><b><a href="/wiki/Rivi%C3%A8re_Noire_District" title="Rivi\xc3\xa8re Noire District">Rivi\xc3\xa8re<br />Noire</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:162px; top:176px"><b><a href="/wiki/Port_Louis_District" title="Port Louis District">Port Louis</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:282px; top:72px"><b><a href="/wiki/Rivi%C3%A8re_du_Rempart_District" title="Rivi\xc3\xa8re du Rempart District">Rivi\xc3\xa8re<br />du<br />Rempart</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:190px; top:108px"><b><a href="/wiki/Pamplemousses_District" title="Pamplemousses District">Pamplemousses</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:150px; top:292px"><b><a href="/wiki/Plaines_Wilhems_District" title="Plaines Wilhems District">Plaines<br />Wilhems</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:258px; top:392px"><b><a href="/wiki/Grand_Port_District" title="Grand Port District">Grand Port</a></b></div>\n<div style="position:absolute; font-size:85%; left:226px; top:252px"><b><a href="/wiki/Moka_District" title="Moka District">Moka</a></b></div>\n</div>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rodrigues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg/220px-Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg/330px-Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg/440px-Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodrigues_BasalticShore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rodrigues <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a> shoreline</div></div></div>\n<p>The autonomous region of <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a> is located 560 kilometres (350&#160;mi) to the east of Mauritius Island. Rodrigues is a <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_island" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic island">volcanic island</a> rising from a ridge along the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Mascarene_Plateau" title="Mascarene Plateau">Mascarene Plateau</a>. The island is hilly with a central spine culminating in the highest peak, Mountain Limon at 398&#160;m (1,306&#160;ft). The island also has a <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reef</a> and extensive <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> deposits. \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outer_Islands">Outer Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Outer Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Outer_Islands_of_Mauritius" title="Outer Islands of Mauritius">Outer Islands of Mauritius</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Agelega">Agelega</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Agelega">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Agal%C3%A9ga" title="Agal\xc3\xa9ga">Agal\xc3\xa9ga</a> region forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Outer_Islands_of_Mauritius" title="Outer Islands of Mauritius">Outer Islands of Mauritius</a>. It is located 1,000 kilometres (620&#160;mi) north of Mauritius Island. Its North Island is 12.5 kilometres (7.8 miles) long and 1.5 kilometres (0.9 miles) wide, while its South Island is 7 kilometres (4.3 miles) long and 4.5 kilometres (2.8 miles) wide. The total area of both islands is 26 square kilometres (10 square miles). \n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Brandon">St. Brandon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: St. Brandon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/St._Brandon" title="St. Brandon">St. Brandon</a>, also known as Cargados Carajos Shoals, is located 430 kilometres (270&#160;mi) northeast of Mauritius Island.  consisting of a number of sand banks, <a href="/wiki/Shoal" title="Shoal">shoals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a>. The archipelago consists of five island groups, which include many <a href="/wiki/Shoal" title="Shoal">shoals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islets</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Mauritius" title="Wildlife of Mauritius">Wildlife of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png/220px-Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png/330px-Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png/440px-Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png 2x" data-file-width="1298" data-file-height="974" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phelsuma_ornata_-_journal.pbio.1001382.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mauritius_ornate_day_gecko" title="Mauritius ornate day gecko">Mauritius ornate day gecko</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Black_River_Gorges_National_Park,_Mauritius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg/220px-Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg/330px-Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg/440px-Black_River_Gorges_National_Park%2C_Mauritius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Black_River_Gorges_National_Park,_Mauritius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Black River Gorges National Park</div></div></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/220px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/330px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg/440px-Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2096" data-file-height="2240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dronte_dodo_Raphus_cucullatus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mauritius was the only known habitat of the extinct <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a>, a flightless bird.</div></div></div>\n<p>The country is home to some of the world\'s rarest plants and animals, but human habitation and the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Non-native_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-native species">non-native species</a> have threatened its indigenous flora and fauna.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Due to its volcanic origin, age, isolation, and its unique terrain, Mauritius is home to a diversity of flora and fauna not usually found in such a small area. Before the Portuguese arrival in 1507, there were no terrestrial mammals on the island. This allowed the evolution of a number of flightless birds and large reptile species. The arrival of man saw the introduction of invasive alien species and the rapid destruction of habitat and the loss of much of the endemic flora and fauna. Less than 2% of the <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">native forest</a> now remains, concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Black_River_Gorges_National_Park" title="Black River Gorges National Park">Black River Gorges National Park</a> in the southwest, the Bambous Mountain Range in the southeast, and the Moka-Port Louis Ranges in the northwest. There are some isolated mountains, <a href="/wiki/Corps_de_Garde" title="Corps de Garde">Corps de Garde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le_Morne_Brabant" title="Le Morne Brabant">Le Morne Brabant</a>, and several <a href="/wiki/Islets_of_Mauritius" title="Islets of Mauritius">offshore islands</a> with remnants of coastal and mainland diversity. Over 100 species of plants and animals have become extinct and many more are threatened. Conservation activities began in the 1980s with the implementation of programmes for the reproduction of threatened bird and plant species as well as habitat restoration in the national parks and nature reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, The Ministry of Environment &amp; Sustainable Development issued the "Mauritius Environment Outlook Report" which recommended that St Brandon be declared a Marine Protected Area.\n</p><p>In the President\'s Report of the Mauritian Wildlife Foundation dated March 2016, St Brandon is declared an official MWF project in order to promote the conservation of the atoll.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2016, a seven-day fact-finding mission<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12_March_2016_Saint_Brandon&#39;s_Mauritius_Animal_Conservation_Press_Conference_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12_March_2016_Saint_Brandon&#39;s_Mauritius_Animal_Conservation_Press_Conference-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> composed of three highly acclaimed international experts (Professor Henk Bauwman<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> (Ecotoxicology, Environmental Pollution, Bird Ecology); Professor Tony Martin<sup id="cite_ref-Professor_Tony_Martin_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Professor_Tony_Martin-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> (world\xe2\x80\x99s foremost expert on marine mammals) and Dr. Nick Cole<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> (herpetologist; MWF Islands Restoration Manager) inspected the islands to raise awareness about the need to protect the islands and to investigate, for the longer term, the effects of plastic and heavy metal pollution in the Indian Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016,  a documentary was made on Conservation on the St Brandon islands held on permanent lease.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When it was discovered, Mauritius was the home of a previously unknown species of bird, the <a href="/wiki/Dodo" title="Dodo">dodo</a>, descendants of a type of <a href="/wiki/Pigeon" class="mw-redirect" title="Pigeon">pigeon</a> which settled in Mauritius over four million years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> With no predators to attack them, they had lost their ability to fly. Arabs became the first humans to set foot on Mauritius, followed by Portuguese around 1505. The island quickly became a stopover for ships engaged in the spice trade. Weighing up to 50 pounds (23&#160;kg), the dodo was a welcome source of fresh meat for the sailors. Large numbers of dodos were killed for food. Later, when the Dutch used the island as a penal colony, new species were introduced to the island. <a href="/wiki/Rat" title="Rat">Rats</a>, pigs, and <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">monkeys</a> ate dodo eggs in the ground nests. The combination of human exploitation and introduced species significantly reduced the dodo population. Within 100 years of the arrival of humans on Mauritius, the once abundant dodo became a rare bird. The last one was killed in 1681.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The dodo is prominently featured as a (heraldic) <a href="/wiki/Supporter" title="Supporter">supporter</a> of the national <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Mauritius" title="Coat of arms of Mauritius">coat of arms of Mauritius</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_and_climate">Environment and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environment and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_beach.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/300px-Mauritius_beach.png" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/450px-Mauritius_beach.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Mauritius_beach.png/600px-Mauritius_beach.png 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_beach.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Trou-aux-Biches" title="Trou-aux-Biches">Trou-aux-Biches</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The environment in Mauritius is typically tropical in the coastal regions with forests in the mountainous areas. Seasonal cyclones are destructive to its flora and fauna, although they recover quickly. Mauritius ranked second in an <a href="/wiki/Air_quality_index" title="Air quality index">air quality index</a> released by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Situated near the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Capricorn" title="Tropic of Capricorn">Tropic of Capricorn</a>, Mauritius has a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>. There are 2 seasons: a warm humid summer from November to April, with a mean temperature of 24.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C (76.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and a relatively cool dry winter from June to September with a mean temperature of 20.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F). The temperature difference between the seasons is only 4.3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>\xc2\xb0C (7.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>\xc2\xb0F). The warmest months are January and February with average day maximum temperature reaching 29.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (84.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and the coolest months are July and August with average overnight minimum temperatures of 16.4&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61.5&#160;\xc2\xb0F). Annual rainfall ranges from 900&#160;mm (35&#160;in) on the coast to 1,500&#160;mm (59&#160;in) on the central plateau. Although there is no marked rainy season, most of the rainfall occurs in summer months. Sea temperature in the lagoon varies from 22\xe2\x80\x9327&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72\xe2\x80\x9381&#160;\xc2\xb0F) The central plateau is much cooler than the surrounding <a href="/wiki/Coastal" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastal">coastal</a> areas and can experience as much as double the rainfall. The prevailing trade winds keep the east side of the island cooler and bring more rain. There can also be a marked difference in temperature and rainfall from one side of the island to the other. Occasional <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclones" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical cyclones">tropical cyclones</a> generally occur between January and March and tend to disrupt the weather for only about three days, bringing heavy rain.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Territorial_dispute">Territorial dispute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Territorial dispute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chagos_Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Chagos Archipelago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago_sovereignty_dispute" title="Chagos Archipelago sovereignty dispute">Chagos Archipelago sovereignty dispute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Depopulation_of_Chagossians_from_the_Chagos_Archipelago" class="mw-redirect" title="Depopulation of Chagossians from the Chagos Archipelago">Depopulation of Chagossians from the Chagos Archipelago</a></div>\n<p>Mauritius has long sought sovereignty over the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Archipelago" title="Chagos Archipelago">Chagos Archipelago</a>, located 1,287 kilometres (800&#160;mi) to the northeast. Chagos was administratively part of Mauritius from the 18th century when the French first settled the islands. All of the islands forming part of the French colonial territory of <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a> (as Mauritius was then known) were ceded to the British in 1810 under the Act of Capitulation signed between the two powers.<sup id="cite_ref-real_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-real-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In 1965, three years before the independence of Mauritius, the United Kingdom split the Chagos Archipelago from Mauritius and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Aldabra" title="Aldabra">Aldabra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farquhar_Group" title="Farquhar Group">Farquhar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Desroches" class="mw-redirect" title="Desroches">Desroches</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a> (BIOT). The islands were formally established as an overseas territory of the United Kingdom on 8 November 1965. On 23 June 1976, Aldabra, Farquhar and Desroches were returned to <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> as a result of its attaining independence. The BIOT now comprises the Chagos Archipelago only. The UK leased the main island of the archipelago <a href="/wiki/Diego_Garcia" title="Diego Garcia">Diego Garcia</a> to the United States under a 50-year lease (which expires in 2016<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (May 2017)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>) to establish a military base.<sup id="cite_ref-real_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-real-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Mauritius has repeatedly asserted that the separation of its territories is a violation of United Nations resolutions banning the dismemberment of colonial territories before independence and claims that the Chagos Archipelago, including Diego Garcia, forms an integral part of the territory of Mauritius under both Mauritian law and international law.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\nAfter initially denying that the islands were inhabited, British officials forcibly expelled to the mainland approximately 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Chagossians" title="Chagossians">Chagossians</a> who had lived on those islands for a century. Since 1971, only the atoll of Diego Garcia is inhabited, home to some 3,000 UK and US military and civilian contracted personnel. Chagossians have since engaged in activism to return to the archipelago, claiming that their forced expulsion and dispossession were illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Permanent Court of Arbitration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg/220px-Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f4/Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="257" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Justice_--Diego_Garcia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Camp_Justice_(Diego_Garcia)" title="Camp Justice (Diego Garcia)">Camp Justice</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a></div></div></div>\n<p>On 20 December 2010, Mauritius initiated proceedings against the United Kingdom (UK) under the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_the_Law_of_the_Sea" title="United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea">United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea</a> (UNCLOS) to challenge the legality of the <a href="/wiki/Chagos_Marine_Protected_Area" title="Chagos Marine Protected Area">Chagos Marine Protected Area</a> (MPA), which the UK purported to declare around the Chagos Archipelago in April 2010. The dispute was arbitrated by the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a>.\n</p><p>After lengthy written pleadings by the Parties and a hearing from 22 April to 9 May 2014 in <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, Turkey, the Arbitral Tribunal ruled unanimously on 18 March 2015 that the \xe2\x80\x98marine protected area\' which the United Kingdom had declared around the Chagos Archipelago in April 2010 violates international law. It is the first time that UK\'s conduct with regard to the Chagos Archipelago has been considered and condemned by any international court or tribunal.<sup id="cite_ref-cha_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Tribunal held unanimously that, in declaring the \xe2\x80\x98MPA\', UK violated international law. It ruled that UK breached its obligations under Articles 2(3), 56(2), and 194(4) of UNCLOS. In reaching these conclusions, the Tribunal made several findings. It considered the undertakings given by UK to the Mauritian Ministers at the Lancaster House talks in September 1965. UK argued that those undertakings were not binding and had no status in international law. The Tribunal rejected that argument, holding that those undertakings became a binding international agreement upon the independence of Mauritius, and have bound UK since then. It found that UK\'s commitments to Mauritius in relation to fishing rights and oil and mineral rights in the Chagos Archipelago are legally binding. The Tribunal also found that UK\'s undertaking to return the Chagos Archipelago to Mauritius when no longer needed for defence purposes is legally binding.<sup id="cite_ref-cha_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\nThe Tribunal held that UK had not respected Mauritius\'s legal rights over the Chagos Archipelago. It considered the events from February 2009 to April 2010, during which time the \xe2\x80\x98MPA\' proposal came into being and was then imposed on Mauritius.<sup id="cite_ref-cha_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Tribunal observed that UK\'s failure to balance its rights and interests with those of Mauritius is to be contrasted with the approach adopted by UK with respect to the United States. It noted that the record demonstrates a conscious balancing of rights and interests, suggestions of compromise and willingness to offer assurances by UK, and an understanding of the United States\' concerns in connection with the proposed \xe2\x80\x98MPA\'. Those elements were noticeably absent in UK\'s approach to Mauritius. Accordingly, the Tribunal found that, in declaring the \xe2\x80\x98MPA\', UK had acted unlawfully and in disregard of Mauritius\'s rights.<sup id="cite_ref-cha_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The parties differ on the characterization of the dispute. Mauritius states that its case is that the MPA is unlawful under the Convention. UK argued that the dispute concerns sovereignty over the Chagos Archipelago. Mauritius requested the Tribunal to adjudge and declare that UK is not entitled to declare an "MPA" or other maritime zones because it is not the "coastal State within the meaning of inter alia Articles 2, 55, 56 and 76 of the Convention."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sovereignty of Mauritius was explicitly recognised by two of the arbitrators and denied by none of the other three. Three members of the Tribunal found that they did not have jurisdiction to rule on that question; they expressed no view as to which of the two States has sovereignty over the Chagos Archipelago. Tribunal Judges <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCdiger_Wolfrum" title="R\xc3\xbcdiger Wolfrum">R\xc3\xbcdiger Wolfrum</a> and James Kateka held that the Tribunal did have jurisdiction to decide this question, and concluded that UK does not have sovereignty over the Chagos Archipelago. \nThey found that:<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Internal United Kingdom documents suggested there was an ulterior motive behind the \xe2\x80\x98MPA\' and noted the disturbing similarities and common pattern between the establishment of the so-called "BIOT" in 1965 and the proclamation of the \xe2\x80\x98MPA\' in 2010;</li>\n<li>the excision of the Chagos Archipelago from Mauritius in 1965 shows a complete disregard for the territorial integrity of Mauritius by UK;</li>\n<li>UK Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">Harold Wilson</a>\'s threat to Premier <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam">Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam</a> in 1965 that he could return home without independence if he did not consent to the excision of the Chagos Archipelago amounted to duress; Mauritian Ministers were coerced into agreeing to the detachment of the Chagos Archipelago, and that this detachment violated the international law of self-determination;</li>\n<li>the \xe2\x80\x98MPA\' is legally invalid.</li></ul>\n<p>The Tribunal\'s decision determined that UK\'s undertaking to return the Chagos Archipelago to Mauritius gives Mauritius an interest in significant decisions that bear upon possible future uses of the Archipelago. The result of the Tribunal\'s decision is that, it is now open to the Parties to enter into the negotiations that the Tribunal would have expected prior to the proclamation of the MPA, with a view to achieving a mutually satisfactory arrangement for protecting the marine environment, to the extent necessary under a "sovereignty umbrella".<sup id="cite_ref-cha_82-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Court_of_Justice">International Court of Justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: International Court of Justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>On 22 June 2017, the <a href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a> asked the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> to give an an advisory opinion on the separation of the Chagos Archipelago from Mauritius before the country\'s independence in the 1960s. In September 2018, the ICJ began hearings on the case. 17 countries have been expected to argue in favor of Mauritius, including India, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tromelin">Tromelin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tromelin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Mauritius also claims sovereignty over <a href="/wiki/Tromelin" class="mw-redirect" title="Tromelin">Tromelin</a> island from France, a small island that lies 430&#160;km northeast of Mauritius.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> France and Mauritius reached a co-management treaty in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Mauritius" title="Politics of Mauritius">Politics of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG/220px-Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG/330px-Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG/440px-Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2567" data-file-height="1615" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Government_House_Port_Louis.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Government House, Port Louis</div></div></div>\n<p>The politics of Mauritius take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic, in which the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Mauritius" title="President of Mauritius">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius" title="Prime Minister of Mauritius">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, assisted by a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Ministers_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinet of Ministers of Mauritius">Council of Ministers</a>. Mauritius has a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the Government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the Government and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Mauritius">National Assembly</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Mauritius" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Mauritius">National Assembly of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_Louis,_Parliament_Building.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Port_Louis%2C_Parliament_Building.jpg/220px-Port_Louis%2C_Parliament_Building.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Port_Louis%2C_Parliament_Building.jpg/330px-Port_Louis%2C_Parliament_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Port_Louis%2C_Parliament_Building.jpg/440px-Port_Louis%2C_Parliament_Building.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6592" data-file-height="3192" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_Louis,_Parliament_Building.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>National Assembly building</div></div></div>\n<p>The National Assembly is Mauritius\'s <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> legislature, which was called the Legislative Assembly until 1992, when the country became a republic. It consists of 70 members, 62 elected for four-year terms in multi-member <a href="/wiki/Constituency" class="mw-redirect" title="Constituency">constituencies</a> and eight additional members, known as "best losers", appointed by the Electoral Service Commission to ensure that ethnic and religious minorities are equitably represented. The UN Human Rights Committee (UNHRC), which monitors member states\' compliance with the International Covenant on Political and Civil Rights (ICPCR), has criticised the country\'s Best Loser System following a complaint by a local youth and trade union movement.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The president is elected for a five-year term by the Parliament.\n</p><p>The island of Mauritius is divided into <a href="/wiki/Constituencies_of_Mauritius" title="Constituencies of Mauritius">20 constituencies</a> that return three members each, while Rodrigues is a single constituency that returns two members. After a general election, the Electoral Supervisory Commission may nominate up to eight additional members with a view to correct any imbalance in the representation of ethnic minorities in Parliament. This system of nominating members is commonly called the best loser system.\n</p><p>The political party or party alliance that wins the majority of seats in Parliament forms the government. Its leader becomes the Prime Minister, who selects the Cabinet from elected members of the Assembly, except for the Attorney General, who may not be an elected member of the Assembly. The political party or alliance which has the second largest majority forms the Official Opposition and its leader is normally nominated by the President of the Republic as the Leader of the Opposition. The Assembly elects a Speaker, a Deputy Speaker and a Deputy Chairman of Committees as some of its first tasks.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Mauritius" title="Government of Mauritius">Government of Mauritius</a></div>\n<p>Mauritius is a democracy with a government elected every five years. The most recent National Assembly Election was held on 10 December 2014 in all the 20 mainland constituencies, and in the constituency covering the island of Rodrigues. Elections have tended to be a contest between two major coalitions of parties.\n</p><p>The 2006\xe2\x80\x932014 <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a> ranked Mauritius first in good governance.<sup id="cite_ref-Ibrahim_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ibrahim-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> According to the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> compiled by the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a> that measures the state of democracy in 167 countries, Mauritius ranks 16th worldwide and is the only African-related country with "full democracy".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Office held</th>\n<th>Office holder</th>\n<th>Incumbency<sup Mauritius">President</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Barlen_Vyapoory" title="Barlen Vyapoory">Barlen Vyapoory</a></td>\n<td>2018\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Mauritius"
