Mauritius">Speaker of the National Assembly</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Maya_Hanoomanjee" title="Maya Hanoomanjee">Maya Hanoomanjee</a></td>\n<td>22 December 2014\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Mauritius)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Mauritius)">Leader of the Opposition</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Xavier-Luc_Duval" title="Xavier-Luc Duval">Xavier-Luc Duval</a></td>\n<td>14 December 2014\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Mauritius" title="Military of Mauritius">Military of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg/220px-Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg/330px-Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg/440px-Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3383" data-file-height="2006" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_National_Coast_Guard_helicopter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Alouette" class="mw-disambig" title="Alouette">Alouette</a> class III helicopter of the Mauritian coast guard aboard the <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Arleigh_Burke" title="USS Arleigh Burke">USS Arleigh Burke</a></i></div></div></div>\n<p>All military, police, and security functions in Mauritius are carried out by 10,000 active-duty personnel under the Commissioner of Police. The 8,000-member National Police Force is responsible for domestic law enforcement. The 1,400-member <a href="/wiki/Special_Mobile_Force" title="Special Mobile Force">Special Mobile Force</a> (SMF) and the 688-member National Coast Guard are the only two paramilitary units in Mauritius. Both units are composed of police officers on lengthy rotations to those services.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Mauritius" title="Foreign relations of Mauritius">Foreign relations of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moscow,_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Moscow%2C_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG/220px-Moscow%2C_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG" width="220" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Moscow%2C_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG/330px-Moscow%2C_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Moscow%2C_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG/440px-Moscow%2C_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1426" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moscow,_Nikoloyamskaya_8C5_July_2009_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Mauritian embassy in Moscow, Russia</div></div></div>\n<p>Mauritius has strong and friendly relations with various African, American, Asian, European and Oceania countries. Considered part of Africa geographically, Mauritius has friendly relations with African states in the region, particularly South Africa, by far its largest continental trading partner. Mauritian investors are gradually entering African markets, notably Madagascar, Mozambique and Zimbabwe. The country\'s political heritage and dependence on Western markets have led to close ties with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and its member states, particularly France. It also depends on the United Kingdom as a trading partner. Relations with China and India are strong for both historical and commercial reasons. Mauritius established diplomatic relations with China in April of 1972 and was forced to defend this decision, along with naval contracts with the USSR in the same year.\n</p><p>Mauritius is a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa_Development_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Africa Development Community">Southern Africa Development Community</a> (SADC), the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/COMESA" class="mw-redirect" title="COMESA">COMESA</a>, and formed the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Rim_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Ocean Rim Association">Indian Ocean Rim Association</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Commercial_Court_(4721902226).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Commercial_Court_%284721902226%29.jpg/220px-Commercial_Court_%284721902226%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Commercial_Court_%284721902226%29.jpg/330px-Commercial_Court_%284721902226%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Commercial_Court_%284721902226%29.jpg/440px-Commercial_Court_%284721902226%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Commercial_Court_(4721902226).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A commercial court in Mauritius</div></div></div>\n<p>Laws governing the Mauritian penal system are derived partly from <a href="/wiki/French_civil_law" class="mw-redirect" title="French civil law">French civil law</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="British common law">British common law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The crime rate reduced from 4.3 per 1,000 population in 2009 to 3.6 per 1,000 population in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius" title="Constitution of Mauritius">Constitution of Mauritius</a> states that for purposes of separation of powers, the judiciary is independent. According to Justice E. Balancy,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2017)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> public opinion is characterised by excessive emotional reaction to crimes arousing the moral indignation of the community. The result is a reluctance to give due weight to the liberty of the citizen and the presumption of innocence.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The provisional charge, part of criminal procedure law since 1852, is a practice that allows anyone suspected of a crime to be detained \xe2\x80\x93 sometimes for up to two years \xe2\x80\x93 before being charged.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, the police detained the editor-in-chief and a journalist of a weekly magazine for having "unlawfully published secret news". The chairman of the company was also arrested. In 1995, the Supreme Court found the provisional charge to be null and void, as the offence set out on the provisional charge "publishing secret news" was not known to the law.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sodomy" title="Sodomy">Sodomy</a> (opposite-sex and same-sex anal sex) is banned by the laws of the country. Although same-sex relationships are not recognised in Mauritius, LGBT people are protected from any kind of discrimination, with the Constitution guaranteeing the right of individuals to a private life.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mauritius is one of the 96 countries to have signed the "<a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_at_the_United_Nations" title="LGBT rights at the United Nations">joint statement on ending acts of violence and related human rights violations based on sexual orientation and gender identity</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, condemning violence and discrimination against LGBT people.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mauritians" title="Mauritians">Mauritians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Mauritius" title="Demographics of Mauritius">Demographics of Mauritius</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Mauritius" title="Religion in Mauritius">Religion in Mauritius</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Mauritius<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">0.5\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.3\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg/220px-Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg.png" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg/330px-Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg/440px-Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="425" data-file-height="389" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mauritius_population_pyramid_2011.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">Population pyramid</a> of Mauritius according to 2011 census</div></div></div>\n<p>The estimated resident population of the Republic of Mauritius was 1,264,000 as of December 2016. The female population was 637,032 compared to a male population of 624,176. The population on the island of Mauritius is 1,219,265, and that of Rodrigues island is 41,669; Agalega and Saint Brandon had an estimated total population of 274.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Mauritius has the highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_population_density" title="List of African countries by population density">population density</a> in Africa.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Subsequent to a Constitutional amendment in 1982, there is no need for Mauritians to reveal their ethnic identities for the purpose of population census. Official statistics on ethnicity are not available. The 1972 census was the last one to measure ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Mauritius is a <a href="/wiki/Multiracial" title="Multiracial">multiethnic</a> society, drawn from <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_of_Indian_origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauritian of Indian origin">Indian</a> (mostly of <a href="/wiki/Bihari_Mauritian" title="Bihari Mauritian">Biharis</a>) and a significant minority of <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Mauritian" title="Tamil Mauritian">Tamils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_of_African_origin" title="Mauritian of African origin">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_of_Chinese_origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mauritian of Chinese origin">Chinese</a> and European (mostly <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_of_French_origin" title="Mauritian of French origin">French</a>) origin.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_(5372546759).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_%285372546759%29.jpg/220px-Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_%285372546759%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_%285372546759%29.jpg/330px-Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_%285372546759%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_%285372546759%29.jpg/440px-Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_%285372546759%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thaipusam_in_Mauritius_-_January_2011_(5372546759).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Hindu festival of <a href="/wiki/Thaipusam" title="Thaipusam">Thaipusam</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_Louis,_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Port_Louis%2C_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg/220px-Port_Louis%2C_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Port_Louis%2C_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg/330px-Port_Louis%2C_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Port_Louis%2C_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg/440px-Port_Louis%2C_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3248" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_Louis,_Saint_Louis_Cathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Saint Louis Cathedral, Port Louis</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosqu%C3%A9e_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A mosque in Mauritius</div></div></div>\n<p>According to the 2011 census conducted by <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Mauritius" title="Statistics Mauritius">Statistics Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> is the majority religion at 48.5%, followed by <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (32.7%), <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (17.2%) and other religions (0.7%). 0.7% reported themselves as <a href="/wiki/Irreligiosity" class="mw-redirect" title="Irreligiosity">non-religious</a> and 0.1% did not answer.<sup id="cite_ref-2011_Census_Religion_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Census_Religion-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Mauritius is the only country in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> to have a <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> plurality.\n</p><p>An officially <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a> state, Mauritius is a religiously diverse nation, with freedom of religion being enshrined as a constitutional right.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The culture of the Mauritian people is reflected in the various religious festivities that are celebrated throughout the year, some of which are recognised as public holidays. According to one estimate Mauritians spend an average of more than 700 hours per year\nengaging in religious activities.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Chan_at_the_2010_World_Championships_(3).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Patrick_Chan_at_the_2010_World_Championships_%283%29.jpg/220px-Patrick_Chan_at_the_2010_World_Championships_%283%29.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Patrick_Chan_at_the_2010_World_Championships_%283%29.jpg/330px-Patrick_Chan_at_the_2010_World_Championships_%283%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Patrick_Chan_at_the_2010_World_Championships_%283%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="354" data-file-height="531" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Chan_at_the_2010_World_Championships_(3).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Patrick_Chan" title="Patrick Chan">Patrick Chan</a>, a Mauritian-Canadian athlete of Chinese descent</div></div></div> \n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Mauritius" title="Languages of Mauritius">Languages of Mauritius</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mauritius" title="Constitution of Mauritius">Mauritian constitution</a> makes no mention of an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>: it is both an English-speaking and French-speaking nation. In Parliament, the official language is English; however, any member of the National Assembly can also address the chair in French.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, English and French are generally considered to be de facto national and common languages of Mauritius, as they are the languages of government administration, courts, and business.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The constitution of Mauritius is written in English, while some laws, such as the <a href="/wiki/Civil_code" title="Civil code">Civil code</a>, are in French.\n</p><p>The Mauritian population is <a href="/wiki/Multilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Multilingual">multilingual</a>; while <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Mauritian Creole</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother tongue">mother tongue</a> of most Mauritians, most people are also fluent in English and French; they tend to switch languages according to the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> French and English are favoured in educational and professional settings, while <a href="/wiki/Asian_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian languages">Asian languages</a> are used mainly in music, religious and cultural activities. The media and literature are primarily in French.\n</p><p>The Creole language, which is <a href="/wiki/French-based_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="French-based Creole">French-based</a> with some additional influences, is spoken by the majority of the population as a native language.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The Creole languages which are spoken in different islands of the country are more or less similar: <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_Creole" title="Mauritian Creole">Mauritian Creole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rodriguan_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodriguan Creole">Rodriguan Creole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agalega_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Agalega Creole">Agalega Creole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chagossian_Creole" class="mw-redirect" title="Chagossian Creole">Chagossian Creole</a> are spoken by people from the islands of Mauritius, <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agalega" class="mw-redirect" title="Agalega">Agalega</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chagos" class="mw-redirect" title="Chagos">Chagos</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri" class="mw-redirect" title="Bhojpuri">Bhojpuri</a> which was widely spoken as mother tongue, has been decreasing over the years. According to the 2011 census, there was a decrease in the use of Bhojpuri at home; it was spoken by 5% of the population compared to 12% in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-2011census_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011census-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some ancestral languages that are also spoken in Mauritius include <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_language" title="Bhojpuri language">Bhojpuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">Marathi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odia_language" title="Odia language">Odia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>. School students must learn English and French; they also have the option to study Asian languages and Creole. The medium of instruction varies from school to school but is usually Creole, French and English.\n</p><p>Although the Dutch were the first to colonise Mauritius and were present for more than 70 years in the 17th and early 18th centuries, today <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> is no longer spoken in the country, and the only traces of the language can be found in old historical documents and inscriptions.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mauritius had a life expectancy of 75.17 years in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> 39% of Mauritian men smoked in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> 12.9% of men and 23% of women were obese in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-who.int_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who.int-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Drugs_in_Mauritius" title="Drugs in Mauritius">Drugs in Mauritius</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mauritius" title="Education in Mauritius">Education in Mauritius</a></div>\n<p>The education system in Mauritius consists of pre-primary, primary, secondary and tertiary sectors. The education structure consists of two to three years of pre-primary school, six years of primary schooling leading to the Primary School Achievement Certificate, five years of secondary education leading to the School Certificate, and two years of higher secondary ending with the Higher School Certificate. Secondary schools have "college" as part of their title.  The government of Mauritius provides <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a> to its citizens from pre-primary to tertiary level. In 2013 government expenditure on education was estimated at about Rs 13,584 million, representing 13% of total expenditure.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/O-Level" class="mw-redirect" title="O-Level">O-Level</a> and <a href="/wiki/A-Level" class="mw-redirect" title="A-Level">A-Level</a> examinations are carried out by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> through <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge_International_Examinations" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Cambridge International Examinations">University of Cambridge International Examinations</a>. The Tertiary Education sector includes universities and other technical institutions in Mauritius. The country\'s two main public universities are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mauritius" title="University of Mauritius">University of Mauritius</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Technology,_Mauritius" title="University of Technology, Mauritius">University of Technology</a>.\n</p><p>The adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> was estimated at 89.8% in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-census_2011_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census_2011-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Male literacy was 92.3% and female literacy 87.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-census_2011_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census_2011-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Mauritius" title="Economy of Mauritius">Economy of Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Mauritius" title="International rankings of Mauritius">International rankings of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_(reduced_colour_saturation).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg/220px-Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg/330px-Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg/440px-Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_%28reduced_colour_saturation%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sugarcane_plantation_in_Mauritius_(reduced_colour_saturation).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sugar_cane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar cane">Sugar cane</a> plantation in Mauritius</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg/220px-Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg/330px-Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg/440px-Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1018" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebene_MCB_Building_Aerial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Commercial_Bank" title="Mauritius Commercial Bank">Mauritius Commercial Bank</a> building in <a href="/wiki/Ebene_CyberCity" title="Ebene CyberCity">Ebene CyberCity</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg/220px-2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg/330px-2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg/440px-2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3607" data-file-height="2405" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2011-06-25_15-14-26_Mauritius_Port_Louis_Port_Louis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A harbour with <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yachts</a> in Mauritius</div></div></div>\n<p>Since independence from Britain in 1968, Mauritius has developed from a low-income, agriculture-based economy to a middle-income diversified economy, based on <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Mauritius" title="Tourism in Mauritius">tourism</a>, textiles, sugar, and financial services. The economic history of Mauritius since independence has been called "the Mauritian Miracle" and the "success of Africa" (Romer, 1992; Frankel, 2010; Stiglitz, 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In recent years, information and communication technology, seafood, hospitality and property development, healthcare, renewable energy, and <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Mauritius" title="Education in Mauritius">education</a> and training have emerged as important sectors, attracting substantial investment from both local and foreign investors.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mauritius has no exploitable <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> and therefore depends on imported petroleum products to meet most of its energy requirements. Local and renewable energy sources are biomass, hydro, solar and wind energy.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Mauritius has one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zones</a> in the world, and in 2012 the government announced its intention to develop the marine economy.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mauritius is ranked high in terms of economic competitiveness, a friendly investment climate, good governance and a free economy.<sup id="cite_ref-imf_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-heritage_foundation_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heritage_foundation-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-State.gov_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State.gov-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doing_business_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doing_business-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The Gross Domestic Product (PPP) was estimated at US$22.025 billion in 2014, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP (PPP) per capita</a> was over US$16,820, one of the highest in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-heritage_foundation_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heritage_foundation-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-State.gov_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State.gov-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doing_business_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doing_business-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mauritius has an <i>upper middle income economy</i>, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The World Bank\'s 2018 <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_Doing_Business_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Ease of Doing Business Index">Ease of Doing Business Index</a> ranks Mauritius 25th worldwide out of 190 economies in terms of ease of doing business.<sup id="cite_ref-Doing_business_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doing_business-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> According to the Mauritian Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the country\'s challenges are heavy reliance on a few industry sectors, high brain drain, scarcity of skilled labour, ageing population and inefficient public companies and para-statal bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mauritius has built its success on a free market economy. According to the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>, Mauritius is ranked as having the 8th most free economy in the world, and the highest score in investment freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The report\'s ranking of 183 countries is based on measures of economic openness, regulatory efficiency, rule of law, and competitiveness.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg/220px-Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg/330px-Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg/440px-Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ile_maurice_1423a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Antique ship models are a prominent souvenir and export of Mauritius</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Mauritius" title="Tourism in Mauritius">Tourism in Mauritius</a></div>\n<p>Mauritius is a major tourist destination, ranking 3rd in the region and 56th globally.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> It enjoys a tropical climate with clear warm sea waters, beaches, tropical fauna and flora complemented by a multi-ethnic and cultural population.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Mauritius received the World\'s Leading Island Destination award for the third time and World\'s Best Beach at the World Travel Awards in January 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tourists can now climb the <a href="/wiki/Le_Morne_Brabant" title="Le Morne Brabant">Le Morne Brabant</a> mountain, which is listed as a UNESCO World Heritage Site.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Issues often encountered by foreign tourists include scams, overcharging and dual pricing.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Mauritius" title="Transport in Mauritius">Transport in Mauritius</a></div>\n<p>Since 2005 public bus transport in Mauritius is free of charge for students, people with disabilities and senior citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> There are currently no railways in Mauritius, former privately owned industrial railways having been abandoned.\n</p><p>The harbour of <a href="/wiki/Port_Louis" title="Port Louis">Port Louis</a> handles international trade as well as a cruise terminal. The sole international airport for civil aviation is <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seewoosagur_Ramgoolam_International_Airport" title="Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam International Airport">Sir Seewoosagur Ramgoolam International Airport</a>, which also serves as the home operating base for the national airline <a href="/wiki/Air_Mauritius" title="Air Mauritius">Air Mauritius</a>; the airport authority inaugurated a new passenger terminal in September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Another airport is the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Ga%C3%ABtan_Duval_Airport" title="Sir Ga\xc3\xabtan Duval Airport">Sir Ga\xc3\xabtan Duval Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rodrigues" title="Rodrigues">Rodrigues</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Financial services is one of the growing sectors of the economy.  Mauritius has an outsize offshore sector which it built on a low tax regime and extensive treaty network.  Mauritius accounted for 42 per cent of India\xe2\x80\x99s foreign direct investment between 2000 and 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Mauritius" title="Culture of Mauritius">Culture of Mauritius</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The distinctive architecture of Mauritius reflects the island nation\xe2\x80\x99s history as a colonial trade base connecting Europe with the East. Styles and forms introduced by Dutch, French, and British settlers from the seventeenth century onward, mixed with influences from India and East Africa, resulted in a unique hybrid architecture of international historic, social, and artistic significance. Mauritian structures present a variety of designs, materials, and decorative elements that are unique to the country and inform the historical context of the Indian Ocean and European colonialism.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Decades of political, social, and economic change have resulted in the routine destruction of Mauritian architectural heritage. Between 1960 and 1980, the historic homes of the island\xe2\x80\x99s high grounds, known locally as campagnes, disappeared at alarming rates. More recent years have witnessed the demolition of plantations, residences, and civic buildings as they have been cleared or drastically renovated for new developments to serve an expanding tourism industry. The capital city of Port Louis remained relatively unchanged until the mid-1990s, yet now reflects the irreversible damage that has been inflicted on its built heritage. Rising land values are pitted against the cultural value of historic structures in Mauritius, while the prohibitive costs of maintenance and the steady decline in traditional building skills make it harder to invest in preservation.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The general populace historically lived in what are termed creole houses.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n\t<li class="gallerycaption">Architectural heritage of class="gallerytext">\n<p>The Plaza, an <a href="/wiki/Art_deco" class="mw-redirect" title="Art deco">art deco</a> theater\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mauritian_literature" title="Mauritian literature">Mauritian literature</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th,_2008-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th%2C_2008-3.jpg/170px-Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th%2C_2008-3.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th%2C_2008-3.jpg/255px-Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th%2C_2008-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th%2C_2008-3.jpg/340px-Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th%2C_2008-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="968" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio-press_conference_Dec_06th,_2008-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Gustave_Le_Cl%C3%A9zio" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean-Marie Gustave Le Cl\xc3\xa9zio">Jean-Marie Gustave Le Cl\xc3\xa9zio</a>, a French Nobel laureate of Mauritian descent</div></div></div>\n<p>Prominent Mauritian writers include <a href="/wiki/Marie-Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Humbert" title="Marie-Th\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa8se Humbert">Marie-Th\xc3\xa9r\xc3\xa8se Humbert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_de_Chazal" title="Malcolm de Chazal">Malcolm de Chazal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ananda_Devi" title="Ananda Devi">Ananda Devi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenaz_Patel" title="Shenaz Patel">Shenaz Patel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khal_Torabully" title="Khal Torabully">Khal Torabully</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._M._G._Le_Cl%C3%A9zio" title="J. M. G. Le Cl\xc3\xa9zio">J. M. G. Le Cl\xc3\xa9zio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aqiil_Gopee" title="Aqiil Gopee">Aqiil Gopee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dev_Virahsawmy" title="Dev Virahsawmy">Dev Virahsawmy</a>.\n</p><p>J. M. G. Le Cl\xc3\xa9zio, who won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_for_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize for Literature">Nobel Prize for Literature</a> in 2008, is of Mauritian heritage and holds dual French-Mauritian citizenship.\n</p><p>The island plays host to the Le Prince Maurice Prize. In keeping with the island\'s literary culture the prize alternates on a yearly basis between English-speaking and French-speaking writers.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Mauritius" title="Football in Mauritius">Football in Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Racing_(Unsplash).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Racing_%28Unsplash%29.jpg/220px-Racing_%28Unsplash%29.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Racing_%28Unsplash%29.jpg/330px-Racing_%28Unsplash%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Racing_%28Unsplash%29.jpg/440px-Racing_%28Unsplash%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4775" data-file-height="2686" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Racing_(Unsplash).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Horse racing at the Mauritius Turf Club, the oldest racecourse in the Southern Hemisphere</div></div></div>\n<p>The most popular sport in Mauritius is <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> and the national team is known as The <a href="/wiki/Dodos" class="mw-redirect" title="Dodos">Dodos</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_national_football_team" title="Mauritius national football team">Club M</a>. Other popular sports in Mauritius include cycling, table tennis, horse racing, badminton, volleyball, basketball, handball, boxing, judo, karate, taekwondo, weightlifting, bodybuilding and athletics. Water sports include swimming, sailing, scuba diving, windsurfing and <a href="/wiki/Kitesurfing" class="mw-redirect" title="Kitesurfing">kitesurfing</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred_horse_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Thoroughbred horse racing">Horseracing</a>, which dates from 1812 when the <a href="/wiki/Champ_de_Mars_Racecourse" title="Champ de Mars Racecourse">Champ de Mars Racecourse</a> was inaugurated, remains popular. The country hosted the second (1985) and fifth editions (2003) of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Island_Games" title="Indian Ocean Island Games">Indian Ocean Island Games</a>. Mauritius won its first Olympic medal at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> in Beijing when boxer <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Julie" title="Bruno Julie">Bruno Julie</a> won the bronze medal.\n</p><p>In golf, the former <a href="/wiki/Mauritius_Open" title="Mauritius Open">Mauritius Open</a> and the current <a href="/wiki/AfrAsia_Bank_Mauritius_Open" title="AfrAsia Bank Mauritius Open">AfrAsia Bank Mauritius Open</a> have been part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="European Tour">European Tour</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mauritius" title="Music of Mauritius">Music of Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sega_(genre)" title="Sega (genre)">Sega (genre)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Theater_in_Port-Louis,_Mauritius.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Theater_in_Port-Louis%2C_Mauritius.JPG/220px-Theater_in_Port-Louis%2C_Mauritius.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Theater_in_Port-Louis%2C_Mauritius.JPG/330px-Theater_in_Port-Louis%2C_Mauritius.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Theater_in_Port-Louis%2C_Mauritius.JPG/440px-Theater_in_Port-Louis%2C_Mauritius.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Theater_in_Port-Louis,_Mauritius.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Port Louis Theatre, one of the oldest opera houses in the Southern Hemisphere</div></div></div>\n<p>The major musical genre of Mauritius is <a href="/wiki/Sega_(genre)" title="Sega (genre)">Sega</a> music, other musical genres are its <a href="/wiki/Fusion_genre" class="mw-redirect" title="Fusion genre">fusion genre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seggae" title="Seggae">Seggae</a> and Bhojpuri songs.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Mauritius" title="Cuisine of Mauritius">Cuisine of Mauritius</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg/220px-Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg/330px-Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg/440px-Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rum_from_Mauritius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mauritius is notable for its <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a> production</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Mauritius" title="Cuisine of Mauritius">cuisine of Mauritius</a> is a combination of Creole, French, Chinese and Indian, with many dishes unique to the island. Spices are also a big part of Mauritian cuisine.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays_and_festivals">Holidays and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mauritius&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Holidays and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The public holidays of Mauritius involve the blending of several cultures from Mauritius\'s history. There are <a href="/wiki/Hindu_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu festivals">Hindu festivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese festivals">Chinese festivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim festivals">Muslim festivals</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Christian_festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian festivals">Christian festivals</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="text-align:left; font-size:90%">\n\n<tbody><tr style="font-size:100%; text-align:left">\n<th style="width: 25em">Public holidays in Mauritius in 2018</th>\n<th style="width: 6em">Date\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year\'s Day</a></td>\n<td><small>Mon 01- Tues 2 January</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Thaipusam" title="Thaipusam">Thaipoosam Cavadee</a></td>\n<td><small>Wed 30 January</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">Abolition of slavery</a></td>\n<td><small>Thurs 1 February</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Mahashivratri" class="mw-redirect" title="Mahashivratri">Maha Shivaratree</a></td>\n<td><small>Tues 13 February</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Spring_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Spring Festival">Chinese Spring Festival</a></td>\n<td><small>Fri 16 February</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/History_of_Mauritius" title="History of Mauritius">Independence and Republic Day</a></td>\n<td><small>Mon 12 March</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ugadi" title="Ugadi">Ugadi</a></td>\n<td><small>Sun 18 March</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a></td>\n<td><small>Tues 1 May</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid ul-Fitr</a> (<i>Depending on the visibility of the moon</i>)</td>\n<td><small>Sat 16 June</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ratha-Yatra" August</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ganesh_Chaturthi" title="Ganesh Chaturthi">Ganesh Chaturthi</a></td>\n<td><small>Fri 14 September</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Indian_indenture_system" title="Indian indenture system">Arrival of Indentured Labourers</a></td>\n<td><small>Fri 2 November</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Divali</a></td>\n<td><small>Wed 7 November</small>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas Day">Christmas Day</a></td>\n<td><small>Tues 25 December</small>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>There are 15 annual public holidays in Mauritius. Seven of these are fixed holidays: 1 and 2 January; 1 February; 12 March; 1 May; 2 November; and 25 December. The remaining public holidays are religious festivals with dates that vary from year to year. However these are public holidays, many other festivals such as <a href="/wiki/Holi" title="Holi">Holi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raksha_Bandhan" title="Raksha Bandhan">Raksha Bandhan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacques-D%C3%A9sir%C3%A9_Laval" title="Jacques-D\xc3\xa9sir\xc3\xa9 Laval">P\xc3\xa8re Laval Pilgrimage</a> also exist in Mauritius.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span not mention any official language, only Section 49 mentions that the official language of the National Assembly shall be English, while French may be used.</a></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
